     174             : 
     175             : // Under certain conditions there may be no-one holding references to
     176             : // a media element from script, DOM parent, etc, but the element may still
     177             : // fire meaningful events in the future so we can't destroy it yet:
     178             : // 1) If the element is delaying the load event (or would be, if it were
     179             : // in a document), then events up to loadeddata or error could be fired,
     180             : // so we need to stay alive.
     181             : // 2) If the element is not paused and playback has not ended, then
     182             : // we will (or might) play, sending timeupdate and ended events and possibly
     183             : // audio output, so we need to stay alive.
     184             : // 3) if the element is seeking then we will fire seeking events and possibly
     185             : // start playing afterward, so we need to stay alive.
     186             : // 4) If autoplay could start playback in this element (if we got enough data),
     187             : // then we need to stay alive.
     188             : // 5) if the element is currently loading, not suspended, and its source is
     189             : // not a MediaSource, then script might be waiting for progress events or a
     190             : // 'stalled' or 'suspend' event, so we need to stay alive.
     191             : // If we're already suspended then (all other conditions being met),
     192             : // it's OK to just disappear without firing any more events,
     193             : // since we have the freedom to remain suspended indefinitely. Note
     194             : // that we could use this 'suspended' loophole to garbage-collect a suspended
     195             : // element in case 4 even if it had 'autoplay' set, but we choose not to.
     196             : // If someone throws away all references to a loading 'autoplay' element
     197             : // sound should still eventually play.
     198             : // 6) If the source is a MediaSource, most loading events will not fire unless
     199             : // appendBuffer() is called on a SourceBuffer, in which case something is
     200             : // already referencing the SourceBuffer, which keeps the associated media
     201             : // element alive. Further, a MediaSource will never time out the resource
     202             : // fetch, and so should not keep the media element alive if it is
     203             : // unreferenced. A pending 'stalled' event keeps the media element alive.
     204             : //
     205             : // Media elements owned by inactive documents (i.e. documents not contained in any
     206             : // document viewer) should never hold a self-reference because none of the
     207             : // above conditions are allowed: the element will stop loading and playing
     208             : // and never resume loading or playing unless its owner document changes to
     209             : // an active document (which can only happen if there is an external reference
     210             : // to the element).
     211             : // Media elements with no owner doc should be able to hold a self-reference.
     212             : // Something native must have created the element and may expect it to
     213             : // stay alive to play.
     214             : 
     215             : // It's very important that any change in state which could change the value of
     216             : // needSelfReference in AddRemoveSelfReference be followed by a call to
     217             : // AddRemoveSelfReference before this element could die!
     218             : // It's especially important if needSelfReference would change to 'true',
     219             : // since if we neglect to add a self-reference, this element might be
     220             : // garbage collected while there are still event listeners that should
     221             : // receive events. If we neglect to remove the self-reference then the element
     222             : // just lives longer than it needs to.
     223             :

    1075             :   float mAudioChannelVolume;

    1077             :   bool mPlayingThroughTheAudioChannel;
    1078             :   // True if the sound is being captured by the window.
    1079             :   bool mAudioCapturedByWindow;
    1080             :   // We have different kinds of suspended cases,
    1081             :   // - SUSPENDED_PAUSE
    1082             :   // It's used when we temporary lost platform audio focus. MediaElement can
    1083             :   // only be resumed when we gain the audio focus again.
    1084             :   // - SUSPENDED_PAUSE_DISPOSABLE
    1085             :   // It's used when user press the pause button on the remote media-control.
    1086             :   // MediaElement can be resumed by remote media-control or via play().
    1087             :   // - SUSPENDED_BLOCK
    1088             :   // It's used to reduce the power consumption, we won't play the auto-play
    1089             :   // audio/video in the page we have never visited before. MediaElement would
    1090             :   // be resumed when the page is active. See bug647429 for more details.
    1091             :   // - SUSPENDED_STOP_DISPOSABLE
    1092             :   // When we permanently lost platform audio focus, we should stop playing
    1093             :   // and stop the audio channel agent. MediaElement can only be restarted by
    1094             :   // play().
    1095             :   SuspendTypes mSuspended;
    1096             :   // Indicate whether media element is audible for users.
    1097             :   AudibleState mIsOwnerAudible;
